Materiaal : 100% acryl. FR | Avec Cinereplicas, la magie d'Harry Potter ne s'arrête jamais. Ces gants de la Maison Serdaigle ne sont pas seulement ultra-doux, superbes et dotés de l'écusson de la Maison, ils sont également magiques ! Vous pouvez les utiliser sur n'importe quelle surface tactile telle que les Smartphones et tablettes tactiles. Fabriqués à partir de fibres légères et aérées, ces gants s'utilisent à l'aide du pouce et de l'index pour tous les écrans tactiles existants. Les gants Harry Potters sont supers. Les gants Harry Potter écran-tactile sont encore mieux ! Les Serdaigles sont connus pour leur sagesse, habileté et érudition. Selon J.K. Rowling, les Serdaigles correspondent à l'élément de l'air. Les Serdaigles possèdentdes qualités telles l'habileté, la sagesse, d'esprit et lacréativité. De nombreux inventeurs et innovateurs bien connus viennent de la Maison Serdaigle. Les couleurs de la maison bleu et bronze ont été choisies pour représenter respectivement le ciel et les plumes d'aigle. Les étudiants de Serdaigle sont connus pour leur individualité et ils acceptent des personnes et des choses que d'autres considéreraient bizarres. Ils peuvent également être eux-même bizarres et possèdent des intérêts intellectuels inhabituels. Alors que d'autres peuvent être enclins à fuir et à ridiculiser ces personnes, en général les Serdaigle acceptent et apprécient ces excentriques. "Si vous êtes sage et réfléchi, Serdaigle vous accueillera peut-être. Là-bas, ce sont des érudits qui ont envie de tout connaître." Chanson du Choixpeau Magique Ce bonnet va de pair avec l'écharpe Serdaigle, les gants Serdaigle, la cravate Serdaigle et la Robe Serdaigle pour avoir l'équipement complet de la Maison Serdaigle pour commencer une année riche en magie à Poudlard! Prêts à embarquer avec le Poudlard Express? Attrapez votre valise, votre hiboux et tous vos accessoires de sorcier, vous ferez sensations sur la plateforme 9 3/4 ! Cet accessoire est essentiel pour un costume de: Luna Lovegood, Cho Chang, Sybille Trelawney,Mimi Geignarde, Quirinus Quirrell, Filius Flitwick, Gilderoy Lockhart...

- [Wall Art](https://desprookjeswinkel.be/collections/wall-art): Because bare walls are just an opportunity you haven't taken yet. A room tells you who someone is. The books on the shelf, the objects on the desk, the things they've chosen to put at eye level and look at every single day. Wall art is the most deliberate of these choices — something you hang not because you have to, but because it matters, because it makes the space feel like yours, because every time you walk past it you want to feel exactly that. A metal sign from a world you love. A wooden plaque with the words you actually live by. A piece of fandom that turns a hallway, a living room, a bedroom or an office into something with a point of view. Our wall art collection brings together officially licensed metal and wooden signs, plaques and decorative pieces spanning all our fandoms — Harry Potter, Disney, Marvel, DC, Star Wars and beyond — designed to be displayed, admired and lived with. Robust enough to last, considered enough to give as a gift, and specific enough to tell anyone who sees it exactly what kind of person lives here. - [Peter Rabbit](https://desprookjeswinkel.be/collections/peter-rabbit): He was told very specifically not to go into Mr McGregor's garden. He went anyway. And we have been rooting for him ever since. Beatrix Potter created Peter Rabbit in 1902 in a picture letter to a sick child, and what began as a small act of kindness became one of the most beloved children's stories ever written. A little blue jacket, a pair of lost shoes, a very close call with a watering can — and somehow, in the space of a few delicate watercolour illustrations, an entire world came to life. Potter's genius was in the detail: the careful botany of her backgrounds, the quietly subversive streak in her characters, the way her animals are thoroughly animal and thoroughly human all at once. More than a century later, the Lake District she painted still looks exactly like her books. That is either remarkable preservation or proof that she simply got it exactly right. Our Peter Rabbit collection brings together officially licensed gifts, homeware, accessories and keepsakes — from classic Wedgwood china and collector's figurines to mugs, nursery gifts and keepsakes that carry that timeless, gentle charm into every home. - [Pippi Longstocking](https://desprookjeswinkel.be/collections/pippi-longstocking): She lives alone. She has a horse on the porch and a suitcase full of gold coins. She is nine years old and has absolutely no interest in being told what to do by anyone. Astrid Lindgren created Pippi Långstrump in 1945 for her daughter, who was ill and asked for a story about a girl who was entirely her own person. Lindgren obliged with something that turned out to be considerably more radical than a bedside story: a child who was the strongest person in the world, who kept no bedtime and answered to no , who made up her own rules and stuck to them with cheerful consistency, and who was at all times exactly, unapologetically herself. Pippi Longstocking was not the first unconventional children's protagonist. She was, and remains, the most completely free. What Lindgren understood — and what makes Pippi's world still feel genuinely alive nearly eighty years after it was written — is that children do not want to be protected from the idea of freedom. They want to see it embodied. Pippi embodies it absolutely: the red plaits, the mismatched stockings, the backwards shoes, the horse named Old Man, the monkey named Mr Nilsson, the Villa Villekulla with its garden full of possibility. She is not a role model in the conventional sense. She is something better: proof that things can be different if you simply decide they are. Our Pippi Longstocking collection brings together officially licensed gifts, accessories, homeware and collectibles celebrating the world's most independent nine-year-old — for children discovering her for the first time, for adults who grew up with her, and for anyone who has ever suspected that the rules were largely made up by people who benefited from them. She is the strongest. She is the funniest. She does not require your permission. Naturally, she is beloved.

Cicely Mary Barker's Flower Fairies have been enchanting readers since 1923, when the first volume of her exquisitely observed watercolour illustrations appeared and introduced a world that felt entirely, convincingly real. Each fairy bound to its flower, dressed in its petals and leaves, posed with the botanical precision of someone who had spent long hours studying both the plant and the creature that might reasonably inhabit it. Brett worked in the tradition of Beatrix Potter, Cicely Mary Barker and the golden age of British illustrated publishing — artists who treated the small scale with the same seriousness a painter might bring to a landscape, and produced work that outlasted the decades it was made in because genuine warmth, rendered with genuine craft, does not have an expiration date. - [Margaret Tarrant](https://desprookjeswinkel.be/collections/margaret-tarrant): Fairies in the forget-me-nots. Angels in the apple blossom. A world where the boundary between the natural and the enchanted is exactly as thin as a child always suspected it was. Margaret Tarrant was one of the most gifted and most beloved illustrators of the early twentieth century — a British artist whose watercolour work, produced primarily between the 1900s and the 1950s, captured the particular magic of childhood imagination with a tenderness and a technical skill that made her prints among the most widely reproduced in the gift trade for decades. Her fairies inhabit flowers and dewdrops and autumn leaves with the complete conviction of someone who found the natural world not merely beautiful but genuinely inhabited by something beyond the visible. Her religious illustrations — angels, nativity scenes, the Christmas imagery that made her name in the greeting card world — carry the same quality: warm, precise, suffused with a light that feels considered rather than accidental. Tarrant worked at the intersection of the Arts and Crafts movement and the golden age of British children's book illustration — the same tradition as Arthur Rackham, Cicely Mary Barker and her contemporary Mabel Lucie Attwell — and her best work shares with those artists the conviction that illustration for children should be made with the same care and the same ambition as any serious fine art. The children who grew up with her prints on their walls carried them into adulthood and passed the affection on. The prints have not dated. They never quite will. Our Margaret Tarrant collection brings together gifts, homeware and accessories featuring her beloved illustrations — for devoted collectors, for lovers of vintage British illustration and the particular aesthetic of early twentieth century fairy art, and for anyone who has always felt that the garden, properly attended to, contains considerably more than it appears to. - [Racey Helps](https://desprookjeswinkel.be/collections/racey-helps): Small creatures. Gentle worlds. The particular magic of an illustration that makes you feel, just for a moment, that the forest has always been like this and always will be. Racey Helps was a British illustrator working primarily in the mid-twentieth century whose watercolour paintings of woodland animals — rabbits in waistcoats, mice keeping cosy homes, hedgehogs going about their business with quiet dignity — captured something that the best animal illustration has always understood: that a small world, rendered with warmth and precision, can feel more complete than any epic landscape. His characters inhabit their burrows, their mossy banks and their sunlit clearings with a domesticity so convincing and so charming that you half expect to find the same scenes if you looked carefully enough into the right hedgerow on the right autumn afternoon. Helps worked in a tradition that includes Beatrix Potter, Cicely Mary Barker and the great illustrators of golden-age children's publishing — artists who treated the miniature with the same seriousness a painter might bring to a grand canvas, and produced work that outlasted the decades it was made in because warmth, it turns out, does not date. His illustrations have been beloved by collectors and gift-givers for generations, and the products that carry his work carry that warmth with them entirely intact. Our Racey Helps collection brings together gifts, homeware and accessories featuring his beloved woodland illustrations — for devoted collectors, for lovers of classic British illustration, and for anyone who believes that small, beautiful things are always worth making room for. Quietly wonderful. Exactly as intended.

Rabbits at tea. Bears on seesaws. Mice in aprons attending to things that mice probably don't attend to, but absolutely should. - [Nasa](https://desprookjeswinkel.be/collections/nasa): We chose to go to the Moon. Not because it was easy, but because it was hard. Sixty-five years later, that answer still holds up. NASA — the National Aeronautics and Space Administration — was established in 1958 in direct response to the Soviet Union's Sputnik launch, and in the decade that followed produced one of the defining achievements in human history: putting a person on the surface of the Moon and bringing them home safely. Neil Armstrong's first steps on 20 July 1969 were watched by an estimated six hundred million people — the largest television audience in history at that point — and represented something that had seemed, until the moment it happened, like a reasonable thing to attempt in theory and an impossible thing to accomplish in practice. NASA accomplished it. Then did it five more times. The decades since have brought the Space Shuttle programme, the Hubble Space Telescope's transformation of humanity's understanding of the universe, the International Space Station, the Mars rovers — Spirit, Opportunity, Curiosity, Perseverance — the Voyager probes now travelling beyond the solar system, the James Webb Space Telescope producing images of the early universe with a clarity that makes cosmologists go quiet, and the Artemis programme returning humans to the Moon. NASA's aesthetic — the Worm logo, the meatball insignia, the flight suit orange, the photographs of Earth from space — has become one of the most beloved and widely worn in the world. The science earned it. Our NASA collection brings together officially licensed apparel, accessories, homeware and gifts celebrating humanity's most ambitious scientific endeavour — for space enthusiasts, for science advocates, and for anyone who looks up at a clear night sky and feels the appropriate combination of wonder and insignificance. We are made of star stuff. NASA keeps reminding us how extraordinary that is.

- [Snoopy](https://desprookjeswinkel.be/collections/snoopy): Good grief. Has it really been over seventy years? Charles M. Schulz introduced Snoopy in the second Peanuts strip ever published, on 4 October 1950, and what began as Charlie Brown's quietly opinionated beagle became, over the following half century, one of the most recognisable and beloved characters in the history of popular culture. Snoopy defies easy description because he contains multitudes: he is a World War One Flying Ace battling the Red Baron from the roof of his kennel; he is a novelist of great ambition and considerable rejection; he is a dancer, a tennis champion, a faithful companion and an entirely unreliable one; he is, above all, a creature of magnificent inner life who regards the world with a mixture of warmth and bemusement that feels, after all this time, deeply correct. Peanuts at its best — and Schulz kept it at its best for fifty years, writing and drawing every strip himself until his death in 2000 — is not really a comic strip about children. It is a comic strip about the human condition, delivered by a cast of children and one extraordinary dog. The melancholy is real. The joy is real. And Snoopy, lying on top of his kennel watching clouds, embodies both at once with complete ease. Our Snoopy collection brings together officially licensed figures, apparel, accessories, homeware and gifts celebrating the world's most beloved beagle and his friends — from Snoopy and Woodstock Funko Pops and collector's pieces to mugs, plush toys, prints and keepsakes for fans of every age and every era of Peanuts. Mickey Mouse made his first sound appearance on 18 November 1928 in Steamboat Willie — a short film that announced both the character and the arrival of synchronised sound in animation simultaneously, which is quite an entrance for a mouse from Walt Disney's imagination. Mickey is not simply Disney's first character. Mickey has been cheerful, mischievous, brave, resourceful and occasionally exasperated across thousands of films, shorts, television series, theme park appearances and pieces of merchandise spanning nearly a century. He has worn a sorcerer's hat, conducted orchestras, gone to space, celebrated every Christmas and been present at the opening of every Disney park ever built. He is, in the most complete sense of the word, everywhere — and has managed, all the while, to remain genuinely charming about it. Sesame Street first aired on 10 November 1969 and set out to do something that had never been attempted on that scale before: use the techniques of television  — repetition, music, humour, short sharp segments — to teach pre-school children letters, numbers and, crucially, how to treat one another. It worked beyond anyone's expectations. Over fifty years, more than four thousand episodes and broadcasts in over a hundred and fifty countries, Sesame Street has educated and delighted more children than any other programme in television history. - [Spider-Man](https://desprookjeswinkel.be/collections/spider-man): With great power comes great responsibility. Nobody asked for the power. He got it anyway, and chose to be responsible about it. That is, in essence, the whole of Spider-Man. Peter Parker was a fifteen-year-old science student from Queens, New York when a radioactive spider bite changed his life irrevocably — and Marvel Comics changed superhero fiction alongside it. Stan Lee and Steve Ditko created Spider-Man in 1962 as something genuinely new: a hero who was also an awkward, grieving, financially struggling teenager trying to do the right thing while failing chemistry and missing rent. The supervillains were one problem. Being Peter Parker was, on many days, the bigger one. That tension — between the extraordinary and the painfully ordinary — is why Spider-Man has remained Marvel's most beloved character for over sixty years and why he translates so completely to every generation that meets him. The films alone tell the story of his reach: Sam Raimi's trilogy, the Amazing Spider-Man era, Tom Holland's MCU Peter Parker, and Miles Morales in the Spider-Verse films, which managed to be simultaneously the most visually inventive superhero animation ever made and one of the most emotionally true. - [Superman](https://desprookjeswinkel.be/collections/superman): He could do anything. He chose to be kind. That, in the end, is the whole point. Jerry Siegel and Joe Shuster created Superman in 1938 and in doing so invented the superhero as we know it — every caped figure, every secret identity, every impossible power set that followed owes something to the man from Krypton. Kal-El. Clark Kent. The Last Son of a dead world, raised in a Kansas farmhouse by two people who taught him that extraordinary ability carries extraordinary responsibility. It is a simple idea. It has sustained one of the most recognisable characters in human culture for nearly ninety years. What makes Superman endure is not the strength, the flight, the heat vision or the bullet-resistant everything. It is the choice he makes, every single time, to use all of it in service of others. In an era of conflicted antiheroes and moral ambiguity, Superman remains a genuinely radical proposition: a being of limitless power who is also, straightforwardly and without irony, good. The Christopher Reeve films understood this. The comics at their best understand this. James Gunn's DC Universe is banking on audiences still responding to this. They will. They always do. - [Miffy](https://desprookjeswinkel.be/collections/miffy): A small white rabbit. A simple line. A world that contains everything a world needs. Dick Bruna created Miffy — Nijntje in her original Dutch — in 1955 in Utrecht, drawing the first image of a small rabbit for his son Sixtus on a beach holiday and recognising, in the simplicity of what he had made, something worth continuing. What followed was over eighty picture books across fifty years, translated into more than fifty languages, with a visual language so stripped back and so precisely considered that design schools have studied it ever since. Bold outlines. A restricted palette of Bruna's own carefully mixed colours. A world of pure geometric form in which a cross of two curved lines makes a face that communicates, depending on its arrangement, every emotion a small child needs to see reflected and every emotion an  is surprised to find themselves feeling in a children's book. Miffy's simplicity is not a limitation. It is the point. Bruna believed that children deserved images that respected their intelligence — clear, considered and completely without condescension. A book should fit in small hands. The text should be speakable as poetry. The colours should be exactly right and no more. He applied these principles to every book he made and produced, in doing so, one of the most recognised characters in the world. Utrecht has a traffic light shaped like her. The Dutch postal service put her on stamps. She earned both entirely. Our Miffy collection brings together officially licensed gifts, accessories, homeware and stationery celebrating Dick Bruna's beloved rabbit — from figures and Funko Pops to mugs, bags, stationery and nursery gifts for new arrivals, for lifelong fans of the books and for anyone who appreciates design that knows exactly what it is doing and does it with complete conviction. Simple. Perfect. Nijntje. Miffy. Both names are correct. Both names are hers.

- [Mouk](https://desprookjeswinkel.be/collections/mouk): Two friends. Two bicycles. The entire world to explore, one country at a time. Mouk is a French animated series created by Marc Boutavant, based on his illustrated books, following a small white bear named Mouk and his best friend Chavapa as they travel the globe by bicycle — arriving somewhere new in every episode, making friends, joining in local traditions, learning something about a different culture and moving on with the cheerful, open-hearted confidence of travellers who have never once found a place that didn't have something wonderful to offer. The animation is bright and rounded and warm. The world it depicts is diverse, curious and generous. The message, delivered with complete lightness and no didactic weight whatsoever, is simply that the world is full of interesting people doing interesting things and the best response to that is to get on your bicycle and go and find them. Mouk understands something that the best children's television has always understood: that curiosity is a value, that difference is interesting rather than threatening, and that friendship is the thing you take with you that makes everywhere else feel manageable. It is gentle, funny and beautifully designed — a show that children love for the adventures and adults appreciate for the worldview it quietly, consistently models. - [Winnie-the-Pooh](https://desprookjeswinkel.be/collections/winnie-the-pooh): A bear of very little brain. And more wisdom than almost anyone else in the Hundred Acre Wood. A.A. Milne created Winnie-the-Pooh in 1926 for his son Christopher Robin, drawing on a real bear at London Zoo and a collection of beloved stuffed animals to build one of the most enduring fictional worlds ever written. The Hundred Acre Wood is small by any objective measure — a forest, a few friends, a pot of honey perpetually out of reach — and yet it contains everything. Friendship, melancholy, the particular anxiety of being Piglet in a world that seems very large, the philosophical serenity of Eeyore who expects the worst and is rarely surprised by it, and Pooh himself, ambling through each day with an appetite for honey and a capacity for loyalty that turns out to be rather profound. Disney's animated adaptations — beginning with the short films of the 1960s and continuing through decades of Pooh stories in every format — brought the Hundred Acre Wood to generations of children with warmth and complete fidelity to what Milne understood: that the best stories about childhood are also, quietly, stories about what we lose when we leave it. The final pages of The House at Pooh Corner remain some of the most affecting in children's literature. We do not apologise for mentioning this. You already knew. You are braver than you believe. And fonder of honey than you admit.

Saban's Mighty Morphin Power Rangers launched in 1993 and produced one of the most immediate and comprehensive cultural takeovers in the history of children's television. Five teenagers with attitude, a wise alien mentor, an ancient evil returning from her dumpster on the moon, and five giant robots that combined into one even larger robot — the formula was, on paper, completely ridiculous. On screen, for an entire generation of children, it was the most exciting thing that had ever happened. The theme music alone was sufficient to cause involuntary air guitar in supermarkets for the following three decades. This is simply a documented fact. What Saban understood, adapting the Japanese Super Sentai footage into something American audiences could embrace, was that the suits mattered less than the people inside them. Barry Allen — the Silver Age Flash, the one most of us think of first — was a police scientist working late in his laboratory when a bolt of lightning struck a rack of chemicals and changed everything. - [Marvel](https://desprookjeswinkel.be/collections/marvel): With great power comes great responsibility. Sixty-five years of stories have been working out what that means. Marvel Comics was founded in 1939, but it was the early 1960s — Stan Lee, Jack Kirby and Steve Ditko in a small New York office producing ideas at a pace that still seems impossible — that created the universe most of us know. Spider-Man. The Fantastic Four. Iron Man. Thor. The Hulk. The X-Men. The Avengers. Characters built from recognisably human anxieties — loneliness, responsibility, belonging, the fear of what you might become — given superpowers and set loose in a world that looked, unusually for the genre, like the world outside the window. Marvel's heroes had jobs and rent and complicated feelings. Their problems did not end when the villain was defeated. That was the innovation. That was everything. The Marvel Cinematic Universe, launched with Iron Man in 2008, became the most financially successful film franchise in history by understanding exactly what made the source material work and scaling it to a global audience across twenty-three films and a universe of television series. Whatever comes next in the MCU, the achievement of the Infinity Saga — twelve years of interconnected storytelling building to Endgame's extraordinary conclusion — will not be surpassed easily, if at all.

- [Nightmare before Christmas](https://desprookjeswinkel.be/collections/nightmare-before-christmas): This is Halloween. This is Halloween. And Christmas. Simultaneously. Somehow it works perfectly. Tim Burton's The Nightmare Before Christmas arrived in 1993 as something the studio system had not quite seen before and has not quite produced since: a stop-motion animated film that belonged entirely to its creator's vision, set in a world so fully realised and so visually distinctive that it required no sequel, no expanded universe and no explanation. Halloween Town is complete in itself — a place of cheerful darkness populated by monsters who are frightening in the most affectionate possible sense, ruled by the Pumpkin King who has everything his world could offer and the particular melancholy of someone who suspects there must be more. Zero is a ghost dog with a glowing nose and the film's most uncomplicated heart. Henry Selick directed. Danny Elfman wrote and performed the songs. Burton's imagination shaped every frame. The result is a film that has built one of the most devoted and aesthetically cohesive fandoms in animation history — one that spans Halloween, Christmas and everything in between, because The Nightmare Before Christmas has always refused to belong to only one season. - [Peter Pan](https://desprookjeswinkel.be/collections/peter-pan): Second star to the right. Straight on till morning. And try not to think too hard about what you're leaving behind. J.M. Barrie introduced Peter Pan in a 1902 novel, refined him in the 1904 stage play that became a sensation, and published the definitive text in 1911 — a story about a boy who refused to grow up, a girl who was ready to, and the island between them where both things were possible at once. Neverland is not simply an adventure setting. It is a psychological landscape: a place where children are free and pirates are the only grown-ups, where time stops and consequence is optional, and where the Lost Boys have found a version of family in the absence of the real thing. It is also, underneath all the pixie dust and crow-crowing, a story about loss — about what is gained by staying young and what is surrendered by it, and about the particular sadness of a boy who watches through the window at a life he cannot quite enter. Disney's 1953 animated adaptation gave the story its most beloved visual form — Tinker Bell, the jealous and luminous; Captain Hook, theatrical and magnificent in his villainy; the crocodile and its ticking clock that is simply the best metaphor for mortality in children's film. Barrie's creation has since inspired musicals, sequels, reimaginings, live-action films and every version of the question: what would you give up, to never have to grow old? Our Peter Pan collection brings together officially licensed figures, accessories, homeware and gifts — from Peter and Tinker Bell Funko Pops and collector's pieces to mugs, prints and keepsakes for fans of Neverland in all its forms. For dreamers, for adventurers, and for anyone who still, quietly, doesn't entirely want to grow up. All you need is faith, trust, and a little pixie dust. We can help with at least one of those.

- [Cinderella](https://desprookjeswinkel.be/collections/cinderella): The dress appeared at midnight. The carriage was a pumpkin by dawn. The slipper, against every reasonable probability, fit perfectly. And none of it would have happened if she had given up. Cinderella is one of the oldest stories in the world — versions of it appear in ancient Greece, in Tang Dynasty China, in the folklore of cultures on every inhabited continent — which suggests it is telling us something we have always needed to hear. Disney's 1950 animated film distilled all of that into something so graceful, so warmly animated and so perfectly scored that it became the template for what a princess story could be. It was also, as it turned out, a fairly accurate description of what Transformers would become. Hasbro's Transformers launched in 1984 as a toy line accompanied by a animated series, and proceeded to lodge itself permanently in the cultural imagination of everyone who grew up in the following four decades. Giant robots from the planet Cybertron — Autobots led by the noble Optimus Prime, Decepticons commanded by the relentless Megatron — crash-landing on Earth and disguising themselves as vehicles. It is, on paper, a deeply improbable premise for one of the most enduring franchises in popular culture. And yet here we are, forty years later, still arguing about whether the 1986 animated film should have done what it did to Optimus Prime. Michael Bay's live-action films brought Cybertron's war to a global audience with rather more explosions than strictly necessary, while the more recent Bumblebee and Rise of the Beasts returned the franchise to something closer to its roots. - [Mary Poppins](https://desprookjeswinkel.be/collections/mary-poppins): She arrives with the east wind, leaves with the west, and never explains herself to anyone. This is, it turns out, the correct approach. P.L. Travers created Mary Poppins in 1934 as something considerably more enigmatic and rather more unsettling than the version most people carry in their heads — a nanny of supernatural capability and zero sentimentality, who dispenses magic and life lessons in equal measure and refuses, absolutely and at all times, to be thanked for either. Walt Disney's 1964 film softened the edges and produced one of cinema's great musical spectacles: Julie Andrews, Dick Van Dyke, animated penguins, a spoonful of sugar and a carpet bag of apparently infinite capacity. Emily Blunt's 2018 Mary Poppins Returns brought her back with elegance and emotional intelligence, introducing her to a new generation without diminishing anything the original had established. What both films — and Travers' books beneath them — understand is that Mary Poppins is not primarily a nanny. She is a force of nature that takes nanny form for the purposes of the visit, which always ends when the family no longer needs her in the way they needed her at the beginning. She does not linger. She does not explain. She simply leaves, with the west wind, carrying an umbrella and a parrot-handled certainty that the work is done. The Banks children are changed. She is exactly the same. That is how it works. Our Mary Poppins collection brings together officially licensed figures, accessories, homeware and gifts — from Mary Poppins Funko Pops and collector's pieces to mugs, bags, prints and keepsakes for fans of both the classic original and its celebrated sequel. For admirers of Julie Andrews' definitive portrayal, for those who discovered Emily Blunt's and stayed, and for anyone who has ever looked up at a departing umbrella and felt something they couldn't quite name. Practically perfect in every way. She already knew.

Strategy games occupy a very particular place in the lives of their players — somewhere between puzzle, storytelling and the quiet, deeply satisfying business of outthinking everyone else at the table. Whether you're building civilisations, managing resources, plotting conquests or simply trying to remember whose turn it is to feed the dragons, a good strategy game rewards patience, lateral thinking and the willingness to lose graciously. Or at least to pretend to. From gateway games that welcome newcomers to the genre and tile-laying classics that have graced living room tables for decades, to deeper, more demanding titles for the kind of player who reads the rulebook before anyone else arrives — strategy gaming is one of the most rewarding corners of the tabletop world, and one of the most social. The best strategy games are not about winning. - [Stephen King's It](https://desprookjeswinkel.be/collections/stephen-kings-it): They all float down here. Stephen King published It in 1986 and produced something that operates on at least two levels simultaneously — a genuinely terrifying horror novel about a shape-shifting entity that preys on the fears of children, and one of the most tender and precise accounts of childhood friendship ever written. The Losers' Club — Bill, Beverly, Richie, Eddie, Stan, Mike and Ben — are among the most fully realised group of young characters in modern fiction. It is a story about fear — what it does to us, how it shrinks us, and what happens when we choose to face it together anyway. It is also, improbably, a story about the particular magic of a summer that changes everything. King has never been better at both things at once. DC Comics has been building one of the most expansive and enduring fictional universes in human storytelling since 1934 — a world of gods and detectives, of alien last sons and billionaire vigilantes, of Amazonian warriors and scarlet speedsters, all sharing the same streets and skies and occasionally the same catastrophic problems. Superman set the template. Batman complicated it. Wonder Woman expanded it into something that could hold genuine mythological weight. The darkness of the stories, the moral complexity of the heroes, the sheer iconography of the symbols: the bat, the shield, the lightning bolt. - [Hogwarts](https://desprookjeswinkel.be/collections/hogwarts): Not just a school. Never just a school. Hogwarts School of Witchcraft and Wizardry sits somewhere in the Scottish Highlands — exact location unplottable, for obvious reasons — behind wards and enchantments that have stood since its founding by Godric Gryffindor, Helga Hufflepuff, Rowena Ravenclaw and Salazar Slytherin sometime around the tenth century. It is a castle that moves its staircases, keeps its portraits in conversation, houses a poltergeist in its corridors and hides the entrance to one of its most important rooms from anyone who is not ready to find it. By any reasonable measure, Hogwarts is not entirely safe. By every other measure, it is home. For the generation of readers who grew up with these books, Hogwarts is not a fictional setting they admired from the outside. It is a place they inhabited — sorting themselves into houses, learning the floor plan from repetition, knowing which corridor to avoid on a Thursday and why the trick step on the staircase requires a particular jump. The arrival letter was real, in the way that matters. The Hogwarts Express departed from a real platform in a real station. And the feeling of belonging that Hogwarts offered — of being sorted and seen and placed exactly where you were supposed to be — has never entirely faded for the people who needed it most. Our Hogwarts collection brings together officially licensed figures, apparel, accessories, homeware, stationery and collector's pieces celebrating the school itself — the architecture, the crests, the four houses together, the Great Hall, the grounds and the atmosphere of a place that has meant something extraordinary to an extraordinary number of people. For every Hogwarts student, regardless of year, regardless of house, regardless of how long ago the letter arrived. Welcome back. The castle is always glad to have you.

- [Weta](https://desprookjeswinkel.be/collections/weta): Where film magic becomes something you can hold in your hands. Weta Workshop was founded in Wellington, New Zealand in 1987 by Richard Taylor and Tania Rodger, and over the following decades built a reputation that is simply without equal in the world of film craftsmanship. The weaponry, armour and prosthetics of Peter Jackson's Lord of the Rings and Hobbit trilogies. The creatures of Avatar. The worlds of Narnia, Planet of the Apes, Blade Runner 2049 and dozens more. When a production needs something that has never existed before and needs it to feel absolutely real, Weta Workshop is where it goes. Five Academy Awards for Best Visual Effects tell part of the story. The work itself tells the rest. What began as a practical effects house has grown into one of the world's most respected producers of high-end collectibles — replica weapons, wearable props, miniature environments and limited edition figures produced to the same exacting standards as the screen-used originals. Every Weta collectible is developed with direct access to the original design files, the original makers and the original intent. The difference between a Weta piece and everything else on the market is immediately apparent to anyone who has held one. Our Weta Workshop collection at Olleke brings together a carefully selected range of their finest pieces — screen-accurate replicas, collector's figures and limited editions from Middle-earth and beyond, for the serious collector who knows exactly what they're looking for and refuses to settle for less. Pieces that belong in a display case, conversation pieces that stop visitors mid-sentence, and gifts for the fan who deserves the absolute best version of the thing they love. Crafted in New Zealand. Coveted everywhere else.

- [Minnie Mouse](https://desprookjeswinkel.be/collections/minnie-mouse): She arrived two days after Mickey and has been equally iconic ever since. The polka dots alone changed fashion history. Minnie Mouse made her debut in Steamboat Willie on 18 November 1928 — the same film, the same moment, the same entrance as the most famous mouse in the world. She has never left, and has never once needed to borrow his spotlight to justify her presence in it. Minnie is her own institution: the bow, the polka dot dress, the white gloves, the heels, and an aesthetic so precisely her own that it has influenced fashion, design and visual culture across nearly a century in ways that are still entirely visible in any department store, any children's bedroom and any Disney park merchandise stand in the world today. What has always distinguished Minnie is her completeness as a character — warmth without passivity, elegance without fragility, style that belongs entirely to her rather than to any trend that might have inspired it in 1928. She is Mickey's partner and Disney's co-founder in any honest reading of the studio's iconography, and the merchandise, the theme park presence and the cultural reach of her image make the case for that reading with complete conviction. Our Minnie Mouse collection brings together officially licensed figures, apparel, accessories, jewellery, homeware and gifts celebrating one of Disney's most enduring and beloved icons — from Funko Pops and collector's pieces to bags, prints, mugs and keepsakes for fans of every age. Polka dots available throughout, as nature intended. Eighty-five years of style. Not a single bad outfit. We are taking notes.

Disney's Dumbo has been quietly breaking hearts since 1941 — a film so spare in its storytelling, so gentle in its animation, and so devastating in its emotional core that it remains one of the studio's most enduring works. A baby elephant born with ears too large for a circus that has no patience for difference, separated from the mother who loves him unconditionally, and befriended by a mouse with more faith in him than the entire world combined. It is a story about being laughed at and flying anyway. About the people who believe in you before you believe in yourself. The Lion King works because it does not condescend. The 2019 photorealistic remake demonstrated the endurance of the story across any medium. The Broadway musical, running since 1997, is one of the longest-running shows in theatre history. The IP endures because the story is, at its core, mythic — the circle of life is not a metaphor. It is just the truth, told at exactly the right speed. Rick Sanchez is the smartest being in the universe and one of its least responsible, a scientist of infinite capability and considerable moral flexibility who drags his fourteen-year-old grandson Morty across dimensions, timelines and the fundamental fabric of reality for reasons that are usually partly scientific and partly because he needs a companion and won't admit it. The jokes are excellent. The existential dread underneath them is real. The fans appreciate both in equal measure. - [Thor](https://desprookjeswinkel.be/collections/thor): He is the God of Thunder. Son of Odin. King of Asgard. And it took losing almost everything — the hammer, the kingdom, the hair — to figure out who he actually was. Thor has been part of the Marvel universe since Stan Lee, Larry Lieber and Jack Kirby introduced him in 1962, drawing on Norse mythology to create a character who brought genuine grandeur to a pantheon of street-level heroes. The son of Odin, wielder of Mjolnir, heir to the Asgardian throne — Thor arrived fully formed as Marvel's most overtly mythic figure, a being of genuine divine power learning what it means to be worthy of it. That question of worthiness — moral, not merely physical — has driven the best Thor stories ever since. Chris Hemsworth's portrayal in the Marvel Cinematic Universe transformed him from a somewhat earnest deity into one of the franchise's most genuinely funny and emotionally complex characters. Kenneth Branagh's 2011 film established the Shakespearean dynamics of the Asgardian royal family. The Russo brothers stripped him of everything in Infinity War and Endgame and found something raw and human underneath. Taika Waititi's Ragnarok reinvented him entirely and was rather brilliant about it. Thor contains multitudes. He would be the first to tell you, at some length. Our Thor collection brings together officially licensed figures, apparel, accessories, homeware and gifts — from Mjolnir replicas and Funko Pops to collector's statues, mugs and prints celebrating the God of Thunder across comics, films and beyond. - [Snow White](https://desprookjeswinkel.be/collections/snow-white): The fairest of them all. The first of them all. And after nearly ninety years, still very much one of them all. Snow White and the Seven Dwarfs arrived in 1937 as Walt Disney's greatest gamble — a feature-length animated film at a time when animation was considered strictly short-form entertainment, dismissed by the industry as Disney's Folly before a single frame had been screened. The world saw it and understood immediately that something had changed. Snow White became the highest-grossing film of its year, won an honorary Academy Award consisting of one full-sized Oscar and seven miniature ones, and established the template for every Disney princess story that followed. Without Snow White, there is no Cinderella, no Aurora, no Ariel, no Moana. She came first. Everything else is downstream of her. The story itself is older than Disney by centuries — rooted in the Brothers Grimm fairy tale of 1812, which was itself drawn from older oral traditions reaching further back still. A young princess, a jealous queen, a poisoned apple, seven companions with very distinct personalities, and a forest full of animals who understand goodness when they encounter it. Disney took that material and produced something that has never once lost its power to enchant. The 2025 live-action adaptation introduced it to an entirely new generation, and the argument about favourite dwarfs began all over again. It always does. Our Snow White collection brings together officially licensed figures, accessories, homeware and gifts — from Snow White and the Evil Queen Funko Pops and collector's pieces to mugs, prints and keepsakes celebrating Disney's very first princess. For lifelong devotees of the original, for fans of the new film, and for anyone who has ever bitten into an apple and felt, just for a moment, slightly nervous. The fairest gift in all the land. Quite possibly.

- [The Aristocats](https://desprookjeswinkel.be/collections/the-aristocats): Everybody wants to be a cat. And honestly, looking at this family, it is very difficult to argue with that. Disney's The Aristocats arrived in 1970 — the first animated feature to be greenlit after Walt Disney's death — and delivered something that has quietly charmed every generation since: a warm, witty, thoroughly Parisian adventure about an elegant cat named Duchess, her three impeccably mannered kittens, and Thomas O'Malley, the most charismatic alley cat ever to serenade someone on a rooftop in the middle of the night. Set against the golden light and cobblestoned romance of turn-of-the-century Paris, it is a film that makes everything look more beautiful than it has any right to. The Aristocats has never been the loudest film in the Disney canon. It doesn't need to be. It has Scat Cat's jazz band, Marie's unapologetic confidence, Toulouse's artistic ambitions, Berlioz at the piano, and a butler villain so incompetent he is almost sympathetic. It has, above all, a sense of style that holds up completely. Some films age. This one simply becomes more charming with time. Our Aristocats collection brings together officially licensed gifts, homeware, accessories and collectibles — from figures and Funko Pops to mugs, tote bags and prints that bring a little Parisian elegance into everyday life. For devoted Disney fans, for lovers of all things French, and for anyone who has ever owned a cat and recognised every single one of these characters immediately. Naturally, Marie is everyone's favourite. She knows it too.

- [The Little Mermaid](https://desprookjeswinkel.be/collections/the-little-mermaid): She had everything the ocean could offer. She wanted more. Honestly, same. Hans Christian Andersen published The Little Mermaid in 1837 as something quietly devastating — a story of longing, sacrifice and love that does not quite save you. Disney's 1989 animated adaptation took that melancholy kernel and transformed it into something else entirely: a sunlit, barnacle-encrusted celebration of curiosity, independence and the specific teenage conviction that the world just over the horizon must surely be better than the one you're in. Ariel is not simply a princess who wants a prince. She is a collector, a scholar of the human world, a young woman of consuming enthusiasms who wants to understand everything and is furious at being told the ceiling is the sea. The prince is incidental. The thingamabobs are the point. The Little Mermaid marked Disney's return to full creative power after a difficult decade and launched what is now remembered as the Disney Renaissance — a sequence of animated films that redefined what the studio was capable of. Ariel came first. She earned it. Our Little Mermaid collection brings together officially licensed figures, accessories, jewellery, homeware and gifts — from Ariel and Flounder Funko Pops to collector's pieces, prints and keepsakes celebrating one of Disney's most beloved films. For fans of the animated classic, for those who discovered it through the 2023 live-action adaptation, and for anyone who has ever kept a collection of things that mattered to them and been told they had too many. You want whosits and whatsits? We've got plenty.

- [Moana](https://desprookjeswinkel.be/collections/moana): The ocean chose her. She would like everyone to know she also chose the ocean, which is an important distinction. Disney's Moana arrived in 2016 as one of the studio's most visually spectacular and emotionally grounded films — a story drawn from Polynesian mythology and culture, set on the island of Motunui, where a young chief's daughter feels the pull of the sea and the pull of her people in equal measure and has to figure out which call to answer first. The answer turns out to be: both, because Moana Waialiki is not someone who accepts the premise that those two things should be in conflict. She sails anyway. She finds the demigod Maui. She restores the heart of Te Fiti. She does all of it without losing sight of the island, the people and the love that sent her out in the first place. Moana is, among the Disney heroines, one of the most complete — a protagonist whose journey is not about finding herself in relation to another person but about understanding her own inheritance and choosing what to do with it. The film's relationship with Polynesian navigation traditions, its visual language of ocean and coral and starlight, and its music — including the extraordinary How Far I'll Go, which is simply one of the finest Disney songs ever written — give it a specificity and a richness that rewards every re-watch. The 2024 sequel and the live-action remake introduced her to new audiences. She handles the expansion of her world with characteristic confidence. Our Moana collection brings together officially licensed figures, apparel, accessories, homeware and gifts — from Moana and Maui Funko Pops and collector's pieces to mugs, prints and keepsakes for fans of one of Disney's most beloved recent heroines. For the adventurer, the navigator, the person who hears the ocean calling and has always planned to answer. The sea calls to those who are ready. She was always ready.

- [Coco](https://desprookjeswinkel.be/collections/coco): The dead are never truly gone. Not as long as someone still remembers them. Pixar's Coco is one of the most emotionally complete films the studio has ever made — a dazzling, marigold-drenched journey through the Land of the Dead that somehow manages to be simultaneously the most joyful and the most quietly devastating thing about family, memory and what it means to be remembered. Miguel, a twelve-year-old boy who wants nothing more than to play music in a family that has banned it entirely, stumbles into the afterlife on Día de Muertos and discovers that the truth about his family is considerably more complicated — and more beautiful — than anyone told him. The film is a love letter to Mexican culture, to the Día de Muertos tradition, to the idea that our ancestors are present as long as we carry them with us. Its visual language — the towers of coloured buildings, the bridge of marigold petals, the luminous skeletons of the departed — is unlike anything else in animation. And Remember Me, in all its iterations, should not work as hard as it does. And yet. Finding Nemo. The Incredibles. WALL·E. Up — whose first twelve minutes constitute an emotional experience that should probably come with a warning. Inside Out, which explained the architecture of human feeling to children and accidentally explained it to their parents too. What Pixar understands, and has understood from the beginning, is that the best stories for children are simply the best stories — ones that work on every level, for every age, because they are about things that are true. - [Luna Lovegood](https://desprookjeswinkel.be/collections/luna-lovegood): She believed in things nobody else could see. She was right about most of them, and gracious about the rest. Luna Lovegood arrives in Harry Potter and the Order of the Phoenix reading The Quibbler upside down, wearing radish earrings and a necklace of Butterbeer corks, and does not appear to notice or particularly care that everyone in the compartment finds this unusual. She is the most fully self-possessed character in the entire series — a girl who lost her mother young, who is mocked by her housemates with a cruelty the books acknowledge without excusing, and who moves through all of it with a serenity that is not passivity but something considerably more difficult to achieve: a complete absence of the need for external validation. Luna knows what she knows. She thinks what she thinks. Other people's opinions of both are genuinely not something she has time for. What makes Luna one of the most beloved characters in the wizarding world is precisely the quality that makes her easy to underestimate: the things she believes in — Nargles, Wrackspurts, the Crumple-Horned Snorkack — are absurd, and she is not. She is perceptive, loyal, fearless in the way that people are fearless when they genuinely do not understand why the danger is supposed to stop them, and possessed of an emotional intelligence that cuts through pretension with the clean accuracy of something that has never bothered with pretension itself. Evanna Lynch's portrayal captured all of this with a lightness that felt completely true. Our Luna Lovegood collection brings together officially licensed figures, accessories, jewellery, homeware and gifts — from Funko Pops and spectrespecs to mugs, stationery and collector's pieces for fans of the wizarding world's most singular Ravenclaw. What makes Ron Weasley essential to the Harry Potter series is precisely what makes him easy to take for granted: he is the human one. Not blessed with Harry's destiny or Hermione's exceptional ability, but possessed of courage, loyalty, humour and the specific kind of steadiness that keeps people going when destiny and exceptional ability are having a complicated moment. - [Severus Snape](https://desprookjeswinkel.be/collections/severus-snape): Always. Severus Snape is the greatest argument in the Harry Potter series for reading to the end before making up your mind. He arrives cold, calculating and apparently cruel — a Potions master with a grudge, a teacher who makes his dislike of one particular student entirely and unprofessionally clear, a man who seems to have chosen the wrong side and never fully recovered from the decision. And then, in the final pages of the final book, J.K. Rowling shows you everything. Every choice. Every sacrifice. Every year of a double life lived at extraordinary personal cost, for a reason he carried entirely alone, in the only form of devotion he had left. Whether Snape's love for Lily Potter makes him a hero or simply a man whose love curdled into obsession is a question the fandom has been debating since 2007 and will continue to debate indefinitely. That is exactly as Rowling intended. Alan Rickman's portrayal in the films is one of cinema's great slow reveals — a performance built on restraint, precision and a wit so dry it could desiccate a classroom, hiding depths that only become clear when the series finally lets you see them. He knew the ending before anyone else did. Rowling told him. It shows in every scene. Our Severus Snape collection brings together officially licensed figures, accessories, homeware and gifts celebrating the most complicated character in the wizarding world — for the fans who defended him from the beginning, for those who came around by the end, and for anyone who has ever appreciated that a story worth telling rarely has simple villains. - [Newt Scamander](https://desprookjeswinkel.be/collections/newt-scamander): He would rather spend an afternoon with a Bowtruckle than at a Ministry function. He considers this a reasonable preference. He is correct. Newton Artemius Fido Scamander — Newt to the handful of people he is comfortable enough with to use the name — is one of J.K. Rowling's finest creations: a Hufflepuff magizoologist of extraordinary talent and minimal social ambition, whose life's work is the understanding and protection of magical creatures at a time when the wizarding world's default response to anything it doesn't understand is to classify it as dangerous and destroy it accordingly. Newt disagrees with this approach. He disagrees with considerable quiet conviction and a battered leather case containing an entire ecosystem of creatures who would not be alive without him. Eddie Redmayne's portrayal in the Fantastic Beasts series gave Newt a physicality and an interiority that made him immediately distinctive among cinematic wizards — the averted gaze, the gentle certainty, the absolute comfort in the company of animals and absolute discomfort in the company of most humans, and underneath it all a moral steadiness that proves, once again, that Hufflepuff produces some of the most genuinely admirable people in the wizarding world. He carries his case. He protects his creatures. He does what is right in a world that is choosing sides and demanding he choose quickly. - [Gellert Grindelwald](https://desprookjeswinkel.be/collections/gellert-grindelwald): He was brilliant. He was charming. He believed, with complete sincerity, that he was right. - [Lucius Malfoy](https://desprookjeswinkel.be/collections/lucius-malfoy): He walked into every room as though it belonged to him. For most of his life, that was sufficient. Lucius Malfoy is one of the Harry Potter series' most precisely rendered studies in a particular kind of villainy: not monstrous, not fanatical, not driven by ideology so much as by the conviction that some people — his people — are simply owed more than others, and that the existing order exists to confirm this. He is aristocratic, contemptuous, impeccably dressed and entirely committed to a worldview that positions him at the centre of everything that matters. For the first four books he operates from that position with considerable effectiveness. Then Voldemort returns, and Lucius discovers that being a Death Eater means something considerably more dangerous and considerably less prestigious than he had managed to believe during the years of comfortable denial. The Malfoy arc across the final three books is one of the series' more interesting studies in consequence — a man watching the world he built around his assumptions collapse with nothing to replace it, failing Voldemort in the ways that actually cost him, and ending the series not vindicated and not entirely condemned but diminished, which is in some ways the more fitting outcome. Jason Isaacs' portrayal — the silver cane, the long blond hair, the contempt barely disguised as courtesy — established Lucius as one of cinema's most watchable secondary villains, a man whose menace came entirely from social confidence and its implications. Our Lucius Malfoy collection brings together officially licensed figures, accessories and gifts for fans who appreciate the series' most elegantly terrible patriarch — and for those who acknowledge, privately, that the aesthetic was impeccable even when everything else was not. The name still opens doors. The doors are fewer than they were.

- [Sirius Black](https://desprookjeswinkel.be/collections/sirius-black): The last of the Marauders. The wrongfully convicted. The godfather who never got enough time. Sirius Black arrives in Harry Potter's story as a name whispered with fear — an escaped Azkaban prisoner, a supposed servant of Voldemort, a man the entire wizarding world has spent twelve years assuming is guilty. He is none of those things. What he is, beneath the gauntness of a decade in the world's most miserable prison, is one of the series' most vivid and most tragic figures: the best friend who survived, the godfather who came too late, the man who finally escaped one cage only to spend the rest of his life in another. Sirius Black is chaos and loyalty in equal measure — the boy who chose his friends over his family at sixteen and never once second-guessed it, the Marauder who could turn into a great black dog and who, even at his most broken, never stopped being exactly himself. Gary Oldman's portrayal in the films caught something essential in the character: the coiled energy of a man who has been wrongly contained for too long, and the warmth underneath it that imprisonment hadn't managed to extinguish. He deserved considerably more time. The story knows it. The fandom has never forgiven it. Our Sirius Black collection brings together officially licensed figures, accessories, homeware and gifts celebrating one of Harry Potter's most beloved characters — for the fans who still feel the loss of that particular chapter, and for those who think a great black dog deserves far more shelf space than he typically gets. Always. In rather a different sense than usual. But still.

- [Rubeus Hagrid](https://desprookjeswinkel.be/collections/rubeus-hagrid): There are professors with more power, more polish and considerably better grammar. There is nobody at Hogwarts with a bigger heart. Rubeus Hagrid arrived on a flying motorbike on the night of 1 November 1981, placed a sleeping infant on a doorstep in Surrey, and wept openly about it because that was who he was and he saw no reason to pretend otherwise. He returned ten years later to collect that same child and take him somewhere he actually belonged, and in doing so became one of the great introductory characters in all of children's literature — the enormous, bearded, tearful guide who leads Harry Potter, and the reader alongside him, into the wizarding world for the first time. We trusted Hagrid immediately. We were right to. As Keeper of Keys and Grounds at Hogwarts, Hagrid's official remit is reasonably modest. His actual role in the story is considerably larger: friend, protector, provider of contraband information, enthusiastic keeper of creatures that have absolutely no business being kept, and the living embodiment of the series' most consistent argument — that kindness is not weakness, and that the people the world overlooks are frequently the ones worth knowing best. His love for dragons, Hippogriffs, Blast-Ended Skrewts and one extremely large spider is undiminished by the fact that none of these creatures have ever made his life easier. Love rarely works like that. Our Hagrid collection brings together officially licensed figures, accessories, homeware and gifts celebrating Hogwarts' most beloved half-giant — from Funko Pops and collector's pieces to mugs, prints and keepsakes for fans who have always felt that Hagrid deserved considerably more credit than he received. You're a wizard, Harry. And Hagrid was the one who said it first.

He said it so many times, in so many contexts, with such complete conviction, that an entire generation of Harry Potter readers says it reflexively whenever something requires attention. Rowling's finest supporting creations — a retired Auror of legendary status, veteran of the first war against Voldemort, collector of Dark wizards and Dark wizard-related injuries, possessor of one real eye and one enchanted magical eye that rotates in its socket and sees through walls, invisibility cloaks and the back of his own head simultaneously. He is grizzled, paranoid, scarred, irascible and completely correct in his assessment that the wizarding world in 1994 is not as safe as people would like to believe. He has the Dark Mark tracking experience and the missing leg and the replacement nose to prove it. The Moody who teaches Defence Against the Dark Arts in Goblet of Fire — vigorous, eccentric, transforming Draco Malfoy into a ferret with cheerful impunity — is, of course, not Moody at all, which makes the real Alastor's eventual appearance and death in Deathly Hallows more poignant than it might otherwise be. The genuine article, glimpsed briefly and remembered through others' accounts, was everything the impostor performed and something beyond it: a man who had spent a lifetime in the fight and not once considered stopping. Brendan Gleeson's portrayal, in the one film he actually played himself, suggested the full weight of that history in every scene. Our Mad-Eye Moody collection brings together officially licensed figures, accessories and gifts for fans who always appreciated the most vigilant Auror in the Order's ranks — and who, on some level, have never quite stopped checking the perimeter. - [Narcissa Malfoy](https://desprookjeswinkel.be/collections/narcissa-malfoy): She never cast a spell in battle. She saved the wizarding world anyway. Narcissa Black Malfoy is one of the most underestimated figures in the Harry Potter series — a woman positioned throughout as a peripheral character, defined by her associations and her family name, who turns out, in the moment that matters most, to be the hinge on which everything turns. In the Forbidden Forest, with the Dark Lord standing over what appears to be Harry Potter's body, Narcissa leans down and asks one question. Not about victory, not about Voldemort's plans, not about the future of the wizarding world. She asks about her son. And the answer she receives she keeps entirely to herself, at the greatest possible personal risk, for the most personal possible reason. That is not cowardice. That is not weakness. That is a woman who has spent years navigating one of the most dangerous households in Britain, married to a man whose choices increasingly terrified her, watching her son drawn into something she could not stop, and finally reaching the point where the only loyalty that remained was the one she had always held above everything else. Narcissa Malfoy loved her son with the completeness of someone who had very little else left to love without fear. It was enough. It was, in the end, everything. Helen McCrory's portrayal brought ice and fragility and something unexpectedly moving to a character the books kept mostly at a distance. She made Narcissa legible — and in doing so, made her memorable in a way that outlasted the films considerably. Our Narcissa Malfoy collection brings together officially licensed figures, accessories and gifts for fans who noticed her, who understood what she did and why, and who have always felt she deserved more acknowledgement than she received. She chose her son. In the end, so did the story.

- [Nagini](https://desprookjeswinkel.be/collections/nagini): She was not always a serpent. That is the part the wizarding world's history books left out. The transformation — from person to creature, from interiority to instrument — makes Nagini one of the most genuinely tragic figures in the extended wizarding world, and it reframes everything that comes later. The serpent who guards Voldemort's secrets, who carries a piece of his soul as one of seven Horcruxes, who strikes without hesitation at his command — she was someone, once. The series acknowledges this late and briefly, but it changes the texture of every scene she is in. Our Nagini collection brings together officially licensed figures, accessories and gifts for fans of both the Fantastic Beasts era and the original series — for those who watched Claudia Kim's performance and needed a moment afterwards, and for the collectors who know that the most interesting characters in this universe are frequently the ones with the most complicated histories. - [Steiff](https://desprookjeswinkel.be/collections/steiff): The button in the ear. The guarantee of the finest. Since 1880. Margarete Steiff made her first felt elephant in a small workshop in Giengen, Germany, and in doing so accidentally invented an entirely new category of object: the soft toy as heirloom. Her nephew Richard added the iconic brass button to the ear in 1904 — a mark of authenticity that has become one of the most recognised quality symbols in the world. More than a century later, every Steiff piece still carries it. Because some things are worth doing exactly as they have always been done. Steiff is not simply a toy brand. It is a tradition of craftsmanship so consistent and so uncompromising that their pieces routinely outlast the childhoods they were made for — passed from generation to generation, kept in glass cabinets, brought out on special occasions, loved in the particular way that only truly well-made things ever are. Their teddy bears, animals and character figures are produced to standards that have not wavered since the nineteenth century, and it shows in every seam, every detail, every button. Our Steiff collection at Olleke brings together a carefully chosen selection of their finest pieces — classic bears, character editions and limited releases that make genuinely exceptional gifts for new arrivals, milestone birthdays, devoted collectors and anyone who understands the difference between a toy that lasts a season and one that lasts a lifetime. For the ones worth giving something that will still be here long after the wrapping paper is gone.

- [Roald Dahl](https://desprookjeswinkel.be/collections/roald-dahl): He wrote for children because he remembered exactly what it felt like to be one. Not the sanitised version. The real one — bored, overlooked, occasionally afraid, and absolutely convinced that the grown-ups were getting away with something. Roald Dahl published his first children's book in 1961 and spent the following three decades producing a body of work so distinctive, so darkly funny and so precisely calibrated to the wavelength of a child's imagination that it has never once lost its grip. Charlie and the Chocolate Factory. James and the Giant Peach. Matilda. The BFG. The Witches. Danny the Champion of the World. Each one a world unto itself, each one built on the same essential architecture: a child who is underestimated, a world that is stranger than it appears, and the deeply satisfying discovery that the adults in charge are frequently ridiculous, occasionally monstrous, and always outmatchable. What Dahl understood — and what his best books demonstrate on every page — is that children are not small adults waiting to grow up. They are complete people with complete inner lives, and they know perfectly well when they're being talked down to. He never did. He talked sideways, through giants and peaches and chocolate rivers and revolting rhymes, and trusted his readers to keep up. They always did. They still do. - [Mulan](https://desprookjeswinkel.be/collections/mulan): She took her father's place in a war he could not survive. She did it in secret, in armour that didn't fit, against odds that were never designed to include her. She did not ask for permission. She simply went. Disney's Mulan arrived in 1998 as one of the studio's most distinctive and quietly radical films — a story drawn from the ancient Chinese poem the Ballad of Mulan, in which a young woman disguises herself as a man to serve in her ailing father's place in the Imperial Army, earns her place through courage and ingenuity, and saves China in the process. Disney's version kept the core of that story and added Mushu the dragon, a cricket named Cri-Kee, and a Huns invasion led by the magnificently terrifying Shan Yu, without losing what made the original worth telling: a young woman choosing honour and family and duty on her own terms, and proving that the terms were never as fixed as the world had decided. Mulan is, among the Disney heroines, the one who earns her happy ending most explicitly — not through beauty, not through patience, but through capability demonstrated under impossible pressure. She is a soldier before she is a romantic lead. The film knows this. The 2020 live-action remake leaned into the martial arts tradition of the source material with striking visual ambition. Both versions have their devotees. Both understand what is at the centre of the story. Our Mulan collection brings together officially licensed figures, accessories, homeware and gifts — from Mulan and Mushu Funko Pops and collector's pieces to mugs, prints and keepsakes for fans of one of Disney's most enduring heroines. For the fan who has always known their own worth, whether or not the world has caught up yet. Dishonour on you. Dishonour on your cow. But mostly: let her through.

- [Department 56](https://desprookjeswinkel.be/collections/department-56): A village that fits on a shelf. A world that feels entirely real. - [Looney Tunes](https://desprookjeswinkel.be/collections/looney-tunes): That's all folks. Except it never really was. Warner Bros.' Looney Tunes launched in 1930 and over the following three decades produced some of the most formally inventive, genuinely funny and culturally durable animation ever made — a canon of short films that were technically produced as cinema supporting features and actually functioned as masterclasses in comic timing, character work and the physics of cartoon . Bugs Bunny, Daffy Duck, Porky Pig, Elmer Fudd, Tweety, Sylvester, Yosemite Sam, Road Runner, Wile E. What the best Looney Tunes shorts understood — and what Tex Avery, Chuck Jones, Bob Clampett and their collaborators built into the form — is that animation is not a medium for children. It is a medium with no limits, capable of doing things live action cannot and comedy that operates at frequencies beyond what the real world permits. The anvil falls. The cliff edge holds until it is noticed. The piano arrives from directly above. The joke works because the universe bends when the scene requires it, and the characters — apart from the brief pause of realisation — accept the terms completely. Our Looney Tunes collection brings together officially licensed figures, apparel, accessories, homeware and gifts spanning the full cast of Warner Bros.' most beloved animated ensemble — from Bugs and Daffy Funko Pops and collector's pieces to mugs, prints and keepsakes for fans of every era. - [My Neighbor Totoro](https://desprookjeswinkel.be/collections/my-neighbor-totoro): He is enormous. He is ancient. He appears only to children and only when it matters. And he carries an umbrella in the rain with the patient dignity of a forest spirit who has been doing this for considerably longer than umbrellas have existed. Hayao Miyazaki's My Neighbor Totoro arrived in Japan in 1988 as a quiet, plotless, almost uneventful film about two young sisters who move to the countryside with their father while their mother recovers in hospital, and discover that the forest behind their new house is home to something extraordinary. Totoro — the great grey forest spirit, part cat, part bear, part something entirely without precedent — does not speak, does not explain himself and does not do very much in any conventional narrative sense. He simply is. He exists in the way that ancient things exist: completely, without apology, as a fact of the natural world for those who are open enough to perceive it. What Miyazaki understood in making this film, and what audiences have understood in watching it for nearly forty years, is that wonder does not require a plot. It requires attention. Satsuki and Mei pay attention to the world around them with the full, unselfconscious concentration of childhood, and the world around them responds accordingly. Totoro is the reward for that attention. He is also — in his rounded vastness, his gentle gravity, his absolute unflappability in the face of two small children climbing him like a tree — one of cinema's most purely comforting presences. There is no villain in My Neighbor Totoro. There is only the world, and the forest, and the bus that is also a cat, and the knowledge that something kind is watching over things. Our My Neighbor Totoro collection brings together officially licensed figures, plush toys, accessories, homeware and gifts from Studio Ghibli's most beloved film — from Totoro and Catbus Funko Pops and collector's pieces to mugs, bags, cushions and keepsakes for fans of every age. - [Resident Evil](https://desprookjeswinkel.be/collections/resident-evil): The mansion. The corridors. The sound of something dragging itself toward you from the other side of a locked door. And the growing, horrible suspicion that you used the last of the shotgun shells on something that turned out not to be the problem. Capcom's Resident Evil arrived in 1996 and did something that survival horror has been trying to replicate ever since: it made a video game genuinely frightening. Not through jump scares alone, but through atmosphere — the deliberate pacing of a Victorian mansion that gives up its secrets reluctantly, the rationed ammunition, the ink ribbons that made saving feel like a decision, and the persistent sense that every room you cleared was only temporarily safe. The zombie — reanimated, lurching, impervious to anything but determined application of force — became horror's defining enemy of its era. The T-, the Umbrella Corporation and the STARS team became mythology. The franchise has grown across nine mainline entries, numerous spin-offs, live-action film series, animated features and a critically acclaimed Netflix adaptation — each chapter expanding the world of bioterrorism, mutated creatures and corporate villainy that Capcom built in that mansion outside Raccoon City. Resident Evil 4, remade in 2023, reminded everyone why it is considered one of the greatest games ever made. Leon Kennedy remains unbothered. Ada Wong remains inscrutable. The chainsaw man remains, unfortunately, very much a problem. Our Resident Evil collection brings together officially licensed figures, accessories, apparel and gifts — from Funko Pops and collector's pieces to clothing and homeware for fans of survival horror's most enduring franchise. For the dedicated player who knows every safe room combination and for the fan who came to the series through the films and stayed for the games. Itchy. Tasty.

Sullivan was coasting on natural talent and Mike Wazowski was working harder than anyone else in the building and still being told it might not be enough. Pixar has always been good at this. Monsters University is very good at this. Mike and Sulley were not friends at first. By the end they are the friendship the first film always assumed they had been. The prequel earned that assumption completely.
